## Gomoku Anti-Cheat Analysis Report: Player X

This report evaluates statistical data from a recent game to determine the likelihood of engine assistance.

---

### **1. Analysis Breakdown: The Signature of Play**

Our statistical models reveal a pattern of play highly indicative of non-human assistance:

*   **Engine Correlation (Temperature MLE):** The player exhibited an exceptionally low `temperature_mle` of **0.045**. This value is strikingly close to zero, signifying an almost perfect correlation with the engine's top-ranked moves. This is a hallmark of direct engine input.
*   **Exceptional Precision (Lambda MLE & Mean Delta):** With a `lambda_mle` of **61.88** (well above the suspicious threshold of 20) and an average winrate loss (`mean_delta`) of just **1.55%** per move, the player demonstrated an extraordinary ability to maintain their win probability. This level of precision is rarely observed in human play.
*   **Statistical Cheating Model Fit (Log Likelihood Ratio):** The `log_lr` registered **14.92**, significantly exceeding the threshold of 5 that indicates cheating. This metric strongly favors the cheater model over the human model in explaining the observed move choices.
*   **Dual Play Pattern (EM Distribution):** The analysis identified a dual-mode play pattern, best fit by a Weibull distribution. **65.0%** of moves belonged to a "Good Player" distribution with an astonishing `em_lambda_good` of **10000.0** (near-perfect play), while the remaining moves, though less precise, still maintained a strong `em_lambda_blunder` of **22.57**. This suggests a blend of near-flawless execution with occasional, but still highly competent, deviations.

---

### **2. Context & History**

*   **Mid-Game Shift (CUSUM Trigger):** A `cusum_triggered` event was detected, indicating a sudden and statistically significant shift in play strength during the game. This often correlates with a player toggling an engine on or off.
*   **Profile History:** There is `no sufficient history available` for this player, preventing a comparison against established play patterns.

---

### **3. Final Verdict**

**Classification: Suspicious (LRT-flagged)**

Based on the overwhelming statistical evidence, this player's game exhibits numerous strong indicators of engine assistance, resulting in a "Suspicious" classification flagged by the Likelihood Ratio Test.

---

### **4. Referee's Advice**

While the Bayesian posterior probability (`p_cheat`) stands at 14.6%, the individual metrics present a far more compelling case for engine use. The extremely low `temperature_mle` (0.045), the exceptionally high `lambda_mle` (61.88), and the significant `log_lr` (14.92) are all powerful statistical signals that unequivocally point towards engine-driven play.

Crucially, the `cusum_triggered` event strongly suggests a mid-game activation of an external aid, which, when combined with the other metrics, paints a very clear picture.

**Recommendation:** Despite the "Suspicious" classification and a `p_cheat` below 50%, the sheer strength and consistency of the individual cheating metrics, especially the `temperature_mle` and the `cusum_triggered` event, warrant **immediate manual review and strong consideration for disciplinary action.** This is a statistical probability analysis, not absolute proof, but the data here provides a robust foundation for further investigation.
